									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Growing up, I have always been surrounded by family members and people who have received and/or pursued little to no education. It is not because they did not want to further their education, but it is due to limited exposure, encouragement, resources, and unfortunate socio-economic and environmental circumstances they faced at that time. The past experiences of these individuals have had a huge impact on my upbringing, and my life altogether. My mom&rsquo;s highest level of education completed is an associate&rsquo;s degree, which has always limited the field of work she could be a part of and advance in. As a single mother of three, it has been hard at times for her to support our family. I have been a witness to her struggle, and I know what it is like to live a limited lifestyle because of it. As a result of my mom&rsquo;s level of education, I have been exposed to a low culturally economic environment, and socialized mostly with people who have not been to college, nor know the aspiration of wanting to go to college. Nonetheless, the community I have grown up in has left somewhat of a positive impact on me. It has not only showed me the alternative to not furthering my education and working hard, but it has taught me to want more from myself and for myself.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Where I come from has had a major influence on the person I aspire to be. I have observed and experienced the hardships people face when they have limited and minimal levels of education and are forced to settle for less. Furthermore, I know the path that those around me have taken is not the path for me. Within my family, I will be a first generation college graduate; I plan on becoming a role model for those in my family and community who are to succeed me. I aspire to study abroad to become exposed to a world I have not yet seen. I also have desires of establishing the foundation for career opportunities, making lifelong friends and taking part in a new culture. I will lead by example, and show the members of my community that there is a way out and an alternative to wanting, attaining and accepting only the bare minimum. By investing in education, I believe you can go wherever you want to go and achieve whatever you want to achieve, which is the message I hope to pass down to future generations. I will be a prime example of what is possible if you take full advantage of your education, and after earning my Bachelor&rsquo;s Degree on May 5, 2018, I am already taking the steps to further my education, in hopes of being an example to the next generation of what academic ambition can allow one to successfully achieve and attain.<br />
&nbsp;I am determined to reach my goals and surpass the standards and accomplishments of those who have come before me. I will not only be benefiting myself out of bettering myself academically, as well as taking control of my life, but I will also be benefiting my community as well.<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In sum, although the community I was born and raised in is not a direct reflection of me, it has helped to shape many aspects of who I am today, and has greatly impacted my aspirations in life. It is because of my background that I have been inspired to continue my education and make my future, as well as the future for those around me, better!<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

Hanoi, Hue, and Hoi An, Vietnam, 2 weeks, vacation<br />
Montreal, Canada, 1 week, vacation<br />
Paris, France, 5 months, undergraduate study abroad<br />

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										As a prospective counseling psychologist multicultural competency is an essential skill I will need in order to adequately provide services for clients I will be working with. One of the most immediate and direct ways to achieve this competency is through exposure and interaction to cultures different from my own, which is why I believe this Social Justice in Thailand opportunity is so important for my growth as a therapist. The field of counseling psychology stress the role of advocacy and social justice, and the first step in meeting that goal is understanding the needs of the individuals we serve. Through this experience I hope to gain an understanding of what social justice looks like outside of the US, in a country that is rapidly developing. I also hope to gain an understanding of the mental health needs and the access to services that can found in Thailand, and how those needs and services differ from those in our country.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
One of the primary reasons I came to the University of Memphis for Counseling Psychology is the program&#39;s focus on International Psychology. Since starting the program I have been actively involved in the International research team within the department, where I was first author on a poster presentation which was recently accepted to the upcoming annual American Psychological Association (APA) conference.&nbsp; Through my continued work on this team I hope to further develop my research interests and dissertation plans to address the mental health needs of refugees.&nbsp; I also hope to work internationally following completion of the program, and having an understanding of how marginalized populations are treated in other countries and the needs these countries have with regards to mental health and social justice will help me greatly in achieving this goal.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
Travel abroad has been an important part of my life since I spent time growing up in Italy after my mother was stationed there as part of her time in the military. Since then I have always been drawn to exploring and understanding different ways of living and different cultures. I was lucky enough to do this in my undergraduate program through studying abroad in France, as well as through my own independent travel. I hope to continue exploring this passion while in graduate school through the Social Justice in Thailand program.&nbsp;&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>

										<span>
										CPSY Social Justice Counseling & CPSY II-Thailand
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-2</span>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-4</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; In 2012, I was afforded the opportunity to travel abroad and experience the rich learning and intricacies of culture dynamics that only a study abroad experience can provide. I was selected from a pool of applicants to engage in intensive one-month study of the African Diaspora and its roots in Paris, France through Vanderbilt University&rsquo;s Black Paris Maymester. This program was a semester-long cultural immersion experience, where I studied the literary, social, and political signifiers of the African-American Diaspora in France. While in Paris, I attended weekly classes at a local school where works such as Aim&eacute; C&eacute;saire&rsquo;s Discourse on Colonialism and Bernard Dadi&eacute;&rsquo;s An African in Paris were critically discussed and dissected by the students. As a part of our cultural immersion, we attended The Commemoration of the abolition of Slavery Event held annually in Paris, France.<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In conjunction with learning about the history of Paris&rsquo; relationship with African countries, slave codes, and current social constructs around race in France, we learned about African-American expatriates such as Josephine Baker, James Baldwin, and Richard Wright. As a part of this experience, we visited Josephine Baker&rsquo;s chateau in Dordogne, and learned about her assistance to the allies during World War II. This experience was my first time travelling abroad, and an incredible learning experience from the moment I stepped onto the plane to leave the United States until the moment I returned to my home soil. My desire for education and travelling abroad did not stop there, however, and I am grateful to have the opportunity to learn from and about another culture, again.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										My name is Asia Amos, and I am an early stage doctoral student in the program for counseling psychology. I am also a black feminist, neophyte social justice advocate, and poet. The reason I state these things first, is because I am not just applying for scholarship funding for a study abroad trip in Thailand&mdash;I am applying for the opportunity to learn, to reflect on my personhood outside of the safe-haven of my home culture in the United States&mdash;I am applying for the opportunity to engage with others in the world and see how they make meaning and stretch themselves to fight for peace and compassion in times of disruption and unrest. The Social Justice Counseling &amp; CPSY II course through which I will be taking this trip, is not a requirement for my program, as there are many other courses I could take to fulfill the electives and multicultural competency program requirements. I chose this course, because of its dedication to wrestling with the complexities and challenges of social justice in local communities and international communities, which will provide me unique insights and perspectives.<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; While my engagements in social justice events and research have allowed me to participate in various local movements and activism, I have yet to expand my involvement beyond the United States borders. Consequently, I wonder, if I can experience enough and learn enough to incorporate global social justice in my research projects, dissertation, and continuing professional life. Training as a Counseling Psychologist requires that I meet both a multicultural competency and social justice and advocacy competency before graduating from the program. What goes unsaid, is that we all have a choice, as trainees, as Counseling Psychologists in the community, to declare our level of involvement in multiculturalism and activism. I choose to believe that social justice and equity are ways of thinking, being, and working throughout the world, over one&rsquo;s lifespan. Therefore, for me, this course does not feel like an option at all, but rather a conscious choice to learn more about the various shapes, sizes, and forms of social justice in the world to better my knowledge of myself, my community, and other communities.<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; If afforded, this opportunity, I will be able to learn about social justice for minority populations in city and rural areas of Thailand. I will gain invaluable perspectives about mental health care in hospital facilities, community centers, schools/universities, and in rural areas where access to care of all kinds is limited for those in need. Through my experience as a student, I will be able to challenge my own beliefs about developing countries, rural populations, and the cultural conceptualizations of mental health care and the lives of those with minority statuses (such as ability, sexual identity). Overall, I hope to return from this trip with an added layer of knowledge and insight about myself, the world, and the work that I plan to do in my dissertation on intersectional feminism/activism and professional career as a Counseling Psychologist.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>
										<br />
I am humbly seeking scholarship support for Advanced Kinesiology Study Abroad in Hawaii. The program is a little over two weeks in length and will be at University of Hawaii in Manoa. I am earning my Master&#39;s in Exercise, Sport, and Movement Science at University of Memphis. I am about to start my fourth semester in graduate school, and I&#39;m halfway through my degree. I am also employed as a graduate assistant. I teach courses to undergraduates and assist with research as needed. I am proposing my research thesis in concussion rehabilitation as soon as possible.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; The Hawaii Study Abroad program will greatly enhance my practical skills in biomechanics and data processing. The purpose of the program is to learn about programming biomechanics software. I will also learn how to prepare a manuscript for reporting the research experiment results. I will greatly benefit both academically and professionally from this opportunity. These skills will make me more employable to get a job after graduation.&nbsp;<br />
As I mentioned, my thesis is concerning concussion rehabilitation. The practical skills I will learn from the Hawaii program will allow me to tailor my research to be advantageous to the population that has suffered from concussion. When I submit my research for peer-reviewed publication, I will be armed with the knowledge of manuscript preparation from my time in Hawaii.&nbsp;<br />
My future plans after graduation are to continue my education at physical therapy school or start a job working in concussion rehabilitation. The Hawaii trip will prove to be beneficial to both pathways. Nothing beats practical experience when it comes to learning. I need to be able to learn how to use the software for biomechanics so that I can study the biomechanics behind injuries.&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />
I am asking for scholarship support in order to offset the costs on my bank account. I pay all of my bills completely on my own. I also have student loans from the previous institution I attended for graduate school. The chance to travel to Hawaii is a very rare opportunity. I started saving and cutting the costs as soon as I learned about this trip. It is true that being able to go to Hawaii is a large reason I am applying for the program, but I will in fact be studying the majority of the time I am there. If I am awarded this scholarship, it will go used to offset the cost of tuition. Or, towards the program cost.&nbsp;<br />
Thank you for your consideration.
										</span>

This course&#39;s overall curriculum will give me a wider base of information to work with for my thesis in data collection, data analysis and processing, and knowledge of taking results and applying them in everyday life/a general population. I feel that this opportunity is unique, and will absolutely benefit me as a graduate student, and later on in my career.

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Statement of Purpose<br />
Travelling abroad to global locales is a life- long goal I have longed to complete. Reading and researching tourism, hospitality and sports cultures in world societies satisfy academic information that leads to graduation, but visiting countries and viewing the lifestyles and the effects of sports management and hospitality, can be a once in a lifetime opportunity.<br />
The Kemmons Wilson School of Hospitality and Sports Commerce are part of a combined curriculum. Both programs promote service operations pedagogy, and implement a philosophy of service management, as well as behind the scenes training in the sports and hospitality fields. I would realize a dream to travel to Coventry, and apply in classes and life, what I learned from the experience.<br />
The University of Memphis offers a multitude of study abroad sites, but The Sports Commerce and Culture in the Global Marketplace program provides real life experiences when understanding the pros and cons of sports programs and marketing in the United Kingdom. Additionally it allows students to learn from seasoned professional who are proficient in areas of sports, tourism, and hospitality in the UK.<br />
Truth be told&hellip; I wanna go to England.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-6</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Financial Need<br />
Academic experiences and life make for well-rounded and capable individuals entering the working arena. With the advent of social media and technology, jobs in sports and hospitality service operations in the twentieth century indicate prolong traveling, living and working in foreign cities and countries.<br />
Dreaming and actually visiting cultures of the world cost money. Parking, tuition, fees, books, and food cost are a few of the demands that exhaust budgets. Therefore, lack of funds curtail travel abroad. The Study Abroad Scholarship will contribute to cost factors inherent for the journey to Coventry. These costs include airfare, medical insurance, passport fees, and spending money. Scholarship monies from the university would help ensure travel to the United Kingdom in July, 2018.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am applying for this University of Memphis Study Abroad Scholarship because I would appreciate the opportunity to study Social Justice in Thailand and cannot otherwise afford the cost of participating in this summer program.<br />
<br />
The reason I would like to participate in this course is that I plan to work internationally as a Counselor once I complete my Master&rsquo;s degree in Clinical Mental Health Counseling. My particular reason for wanting to study Social Justice in Thailand is that human trafficking is something of which I am keenly aware, and I would like to be a part of stopping this horrid and inhumane practice. Through Dr. Ovrebo and this course, I look forward to connecting with local Thai anti-trafficking organizations to see how they operate to assist victims, and move them forward with their lives. I am excited to&nbsp;witness the successful Royal Project, which is&nbsp;assisting Northern villagers to grow organic produce to sell to Bangkok restaurants, rather than growing poppies to manufacture heroin. I would like&nbsp;to investigate additional resources that could help to provide safety and income.<br />
<br />
I lived&nbsp;two hours&nbsp;south of Bangkok in 1998-1999. &nbsp;I had an up-close view of the dark underbelly of Thai society: the sex industry. I lived outside Pattaya, a city often called, &quot;The sex tourism capital of the world.&quot; Prostitution is&nbsp;officially&nbsp;illegal in Thailand; however, due to the nature of Thai culture, most Thais choose to &quot;walk with one eye closed&quot; regarding this profitable industry that exploits and enslaves tens of thousands of children and young people. Part of my interest in this Social Justice program is traveling through Northern Thailand for&nbsp;my first time. This area is a large&nbsp;source of victims for human traffickers who move people from these northern&nbsp;villages to cities to work.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
Thailand has so much to admire and appreciate: its ancient culture, cuisine and most importantly, its people. I believe traveling to Thailand and learning more about the culture and the many disadvantages villagers and refugees face will help me to gain experience and competence in an international&nbsp;counseling setting.<br />
<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>
										1) 2006- Italy (Rome, Florence, Venice)- 2 weeks: Sacred Music module course to fulfill requirements of Bachelor of Music degree at Centenary College.&nbsp;<br />
2) 2010- Novafeltria, Italy- 6 weeks: Young artist program (I was cast in production of La Traviata which toured through the Rimini province.)<br />

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am honored to have been selected as one of six Teaching Fellows with the International Performing Arts Institute in Kiefersfelden, Germany this summer. During this professional development intensive, I will be studying vocal pedagogy with renown performer, vocal coach, and clinician, Maryann Kyle. In additional to my own personal study, I will have the opportunity to further my experience as a collegiate-level instructor by teaching private lessons to undergraduate music students, leading and assisting masterclasses, and stage-directing and music-directing opera scenes. Through the IPAI program, I will also have the opportunity to study the German language for the first time, both formally and immersively. In addition to expanding my skillset as an educator, IPAI has scheduled my auditions with German and Austrian agents and conductors, which is the incredible professional opportunity every American classical musician aspires to have.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
My primary goal in pursuing a Doctorate of Musical Arts is to acquire the expertise necessary to teach at the collegiate level. Unfortunately, the curriculum for the degree itself cannot provide all the resources for DMA candidates to become effective instructors and successful job applicants. The IPAI fellowship fills in curricular gaps, specifically preparing me for success an educator and job applicant.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
In addition to having an extensive performance resume, vocalists applying for jobs in higher education are expected to be proficient speakers of Italian, French, and German. To be competitive, each applicant must also be prepared to give public masterclasses during the interview process, present a cohesive teaching philosophy, and have experience stage-directing. These are all skills I will have the unique opportunity to gain and strengthen during my IPAI fellowship, exponentially increasing both my employability upon graduating from the University of Memphis and my efficacy as an educator for the duration of my career.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

									<td>

										<span>
										To whom it may concern,<br />
&nbsp;<br />
I am applying for the study abroad scholarship because I recognize an opportunity during this course of study to accomplish objectives that are less attainable during the normal academic semester. My advisor has recommended that I apply for this study abroad opportunity, and it is my sincere belief that this faculty representative has my best interest in mind when making these recommendations.<br />
<br />
The study abroad semester in advanced kinesiology promises an intensive technological course load which addresses skills needed for biomechanical data collection, analysis, and processing. Naturally, these are components of thesis and dissertation research projects with which students commonly require a great deal of faculty assistance. My preference is to develop a skill-set which makes me more autonomous with regard to conducting ethical and meaningful research so that my advisors are available to assist others. &nbsp;<br />
<br />
I will have to propose my thesis by the end of the current (spring) semester, and I cannot think of a more timely exposure for the material promised by the advanced kinesiology study abroad course. Beginning next fall, I will need to have begun collecting data for my thesis project and be able to submit on time for review and defense. In my estimation, the only rate-limiting factor in this process is my level of familiarity and expertise with the software used for collection, processing, and analysis of the data I will be dealing with.<br />
<br />
Consideration for this award would be sincerely appreciated and could conceivably give us a shot to get some thesis projects published. It&rsquo;s my understanding that publishing thesis research in academic journals is relatively rare, and often times this is owed in part to lack of robust research oriented skill sets in individuals tasked with carrying out the research. My preference would be to become an exception to this unfortunate rule.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
Alex Carnall<br />
&nbsp;

									<td>

										<span>
										I am seeking scholarship support for my study abroad program, British Studies, in order to be financially capable of attending this program. I am a graduate student with the University of Memphis with the MFA program. This study abroad program will help me develop my reading and writing skills as an academic, and in turn improve my thesis. With the British Studies program, I will be able to study the traditional novel in its original setting. This will give me more insight on literature; knowledge in which I can give to my future students in the Fall 2018 as a Teaching Assistant. The relationship of the study abroad experience and my thesis is British Literature. My comps list and thesis reflect that of the Victorian writing styles. This study abroad program will allow me to research British Literature as well as British writing technique and styles to be reflected in my writing. This study aboard experience is an important addition to my literature and creative writing study at the University of Memphis. This program will allow me to read texts from their original study, giving me the opportunity to understand the authoritative choices of British writers. This program also gives the opportunity to travel to neighboring countries such as Scotland, Ireland, and France to study literature and writing styles in correlation with historic periods.There are very few graduate study abroad programs, especially that of literature study.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">

There would be no cost for research support such as copying or microfilming. All research will be conducted at the university affiliated with the program.&nbsp;

										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The incentive and opportunity to learn about aspects of international law is probably one of the most obvious. Since all of the classes have a substantial international or comparative component, I will necessarily be exposed to various aspects of international law.&nbsp; A consideration of what those materials may include reveals that the benefit is broader than simply an exposure to the kind of international law that is taught in a lot of basic survey courses.<br />
<br />
In the Cambridge program, the focus is not just on Public International Law or International Business Transactions, two of the staples in the curriculum at most American law schools. Instead, faculty members teach international or comparative issues relating to their particular areas of expertise, which does a couple of things. First, and most obviously, this approach offers a breadth of international or comparative classes that is unlikely to be available at most law schools. Secondly, it gives insights into how international law issues can permeate other areas of law. For example, in the 2015 summer session, in addition to Public International Law, students were offered the opportunity to take classes that covered international or comparative issues in corporate law, religious freedom, sports law, law and literature, advocacy and dispute resolution, and legal research. In 2014, the specialized classes included International Commercial Litigation, Comparative Family Law, International Entertainment Law, and Transnational Insolvency.<br />
<br />
Offerings of this breadth allows me to focus on areas of particular interest to them and also provide students with the opportunity to see how international law permeates subjects that they may have taken or later take in the US which might lack a focus on the international or comparative component. As the modern practice of law becomes increasingly global in scope, this kind of exposure is important not only for substantive knowledge but also for the ability to see international aspects and issues that might otherwise be missed. This is more than just resume fodder; it is helpful knowledge for informed legal practitioners.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

I work at as a pro bono student attorney with the University of Memphis Elder Law Clinic, and because of my involvement do not have ample time to secure an additional paying job.&nbsp; This scholarship provides a chance for people who are struggling to further their education, to become the exception and succeed.&nbsp; I hope to become one of those special people and it is with great honor and appreciation that I submit this application for your consideration.&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The purpose of the study abroad program with Howard University is to&nbsp;offer an opportunity for students to witness firsthand the historic legal and political changes in South Africa. The experience that I would gain in Africa would be invaluable; the program offers the opportunity to interact with South African law students while learning about the struggles of the democratic government in Cape Town, South Africa. I selected this program because it will offer me the chance to connect with a piece of my heritage that I would otherwise never get the chance to do; this experience will dispel the negative stereotypes that I may have about Africa&#39;s development and encourage me to inform others of the unique aspects and culture that Africa offers. This program specifically contributes to competence in the legal field because it provides an opportunity for international networking, knowledge of another country&#39;s government and the problems as well as the successes of how it is run. The program offers a course, South Africa&#39;s Constitution, which offers a deep analysis of the country&#39;s governments. Being able to analyze another body of laws will help me to use that information in shaping the legal community in the United States.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am a first semester graduate student studying exercise, sport and movement science in the School of Health Studies. I have the opportunity to travel to Hawaii and study advanced biomechanics and data processing in the Advanced Kinesiology Program. This course will allow me to design and conduct a research study investigating human biomechanics, analyze the collected data and interpret it in a suitable way for peer-reviewed publication. I am applying for this scholarship because my Master&#39;s Thesis will involve data collection and processing of human movement with regard to Anterior Cruciate Ligament Injury in young athletes. My Thesis project will be conducted in a similar manner to the research design in the Advanced Kinesiology and if I complete this course I will gain a large knowledge base to prepare myself successfully.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

The program cost of $2,250 does not include food.<br />
<br />
The tuition cost for graduate level students is $1,825.&nbsp;<br />

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I chose the Accra, Ghana program because I believe it will further enhance my studies in African American Literature. While I am working towards an MFA in Creative Nonfiction Writing, I am also working towards a certificate in African American Literature. After graduate school, I plan to open an Arts Cafe in one of Memphis&#39; impoverished neighborhoods and offer creative writing and arts classes focusing on African American history/literature.<br />
<br />
The Accra program will provide information that my University of Memphis program cannot offer. To actually step upon the ground that my ancestors inhabited before being kidnapped, will be a spiritual as well as a learning experience, maybe even a once in a lifetime experience. I want to learn more about the transatlantic slave trade and what better way to study it than the ground on which it began. My goal is to absorb as much information as possible and write a few essays to include in my thesis, and to share my experiences with the youth that I hope will one day frequent the Arts Cafe.<br />
<br />
The scholarship funds will help make this opportunity available to me, otherwise I won&rsquo;t be able to attend the program. I appreciated your consideration.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										A main interest of mine is international psychology, and that interest heavily influenced my decision in coming to the University of Memphis for my doctoral program. Studying abroad in Thailand will teach me what international work in my field can look like, and I am hoping to be able to apply what I learn to my own work one day. An educational goal of mine is to work and conduct research abroad, potentially through the Fulbright program. This study abroad experience will help me achieve my goal by giving me social justice experience abroad and by potentially making connections while abroad. Additionally, I chose this study abroad trip to Thailand because of its focus on social justice, LGBT communities, and sex trafficking. These facets of the program all apply to my research and clinical interests, both in the states and internationally. My current research projects encompass ethnic, gender, sexual, and religious minorities, and my future projects include work with refugees. Having experience with work abroad in Thailand ties directly to my research projects because of their social justice and multicultural focus. I am hoping to learn more about culturally different mental health practices while in Thailand so I can be more aware of decolonizing mental health care in my future work. I also am excited to learn about sex trafficking in another country as my clinical and research interests with refugees will expose me to sex trafficking in different populations. Another reason I want to go on this trip is to be more culturally competent in my practice. I believe that gaining more exposure to different cultures, especially one I have not experienced before, will make me a better clinician and researcher. Obtaining a study abroad scholarship will be instrumental in helping me achieve my goals of improving as a clinician and researcher, as well as allowing me to work towards my future career goals of working abroad.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am applying for the Temple Summer Law Program in Rome that will take place beginning May 22, 2018 and ending on June 22, 2018.&nbsp; The University&#39;s campus is located on the Tiber River within walking distance of many famous historic sites.&nbsp; The courses that I will take are (1) &quot;Law and Justice: International Literary Perspectives&quot;--2 credit hours, (2) &quot;International Dispute Resolution&quot;--2 credit hours, and (3) &quot;Global Legal Perspectives&quot;--1 credit hour.&nbsp; I am applying for the program because I think it is crucial to have a global understanding of the legal field.&nbsp; It is incredibly easy to just focus on what is around me, but it is much more important to have a big picture understanding of other perspectives.&nbsp; It will be my first time out of the country, and I truly believe this experience is necessary.&nbsp; Upon graduation, I intend to practice immigration law and one important aspect of my career will be to encounter individuals from different backgrounds.&nbsp; I certainly have an understanding of the Latino culture given my family background, but I would feel much more prepared getting an understanding and immersing myself into the culture of another.&nbsp; I selected this study abroad program because of the courses offered.&nbsp; The courses uses literature and case law to get an understanding of different perspectives and the effects it can have on the legal field.&nbsp; It will introduce me to fundamental concepts such as international arbitration and cross-cultural negotiation.&nbsp; I am currently enrolled in a negotiation and mediation class and it would be great to follow the semester up with a cross-cultural mediation course.&nbsp; The courses included introduction to European law, overview of the global legal profession, and international aspects of law.&nbsp; The program also offers opportunities to take part in an internship with Italian Legal Firms during the course of the program.&nbsp; This study abroad program will truly enhance my understanding of the legal profession outside of the United States and will be extremely helpful as I enter my international law courses during my third year of law school starting in the fall.&nbsp; I believe that I will be the most effective as an advocate for my clients as an immigration attorney, if I have a better understanding of other cultures.&nbsp; I will have the opportunity to meet students and professors from other States and Countries and I will be able to learn and understand from them.&nbsp; This is an incredible opportunity and I would love the opportunity to enroll and have financial assistance in the program.&nbsp;&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>2-5</span>

									<td>

										<span>
										The 4-week intensive program at the Alliance Francais de Toulouse will be an excellent opportunity for me to immerse myself in French language and culture as a key step toward achieving my educational and professional goal of full fluency within the language. This desire is two-fold: one, my intention is to pursue career-long research in late-twentieth-century/contemporary French philosophy and critical theory, beginning my doctoral dissertation at Memphis and extending through publications within French-language academic journals; and second, my more immediate goal is to attain sufficient working fluency in order to successfully apply for the Erasmus Mundus Program after I have competed my qualifying and comprehensive exams. In fact, one of the universities that participates in the Erasmus Mundus is the Universit&eacute;&nbsp;Toulouse, so this program would give me the opportunity to begin to develop contacts within that institution. One of the reasons that I applied to study at Memphis was for its strengths in contemporary French philosophy as well as its relationship with the Erasmus Mundus Program, so this program is well-suited to these long-held goals. Additionally, the&nbsp;Alliance Francais is specifically focused on French language instruction, as opposed to other programs that split between language development and other, more general coursework. Because of this design and specialized focus, it is more cost-effective and efficient for my particular academic goals than other programs that are offered through the Study Abroad office. In short, the program via the Alliance in Toulouse would provide excellent avenues not only in language acquisition, but my academic and professional development as well.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-6</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										As a Graduate Assistant for the University of Memphis, my yearly income is set at $20,000. (As the last day of payment is April 30, and the next payment I will receive is September 30, I have to spend at least $3000 of it over the summer for bare costs of rent, in addition to food, travel, and other expenses, rendering my summer budget extremely tight, notwithstanding other expenses.) The cost of the program will be 550&euro;, plus 50&euro; registration and 20&euro; for a host family search, not counting course materials (http://www.alliance-toulouse.org/nos-cours.php?g=intensive-courses&amp;idType=1#date1-61). To stay with a French host family with a breakfast for 4 weeks will be 480&euro; (http://www.alliance-toulouse.org/logement.php) -- a subtotal of 1100&euro;. According to numbeo.com, the monthly living costs for a single person in Toulouse, not including rent, are ~740&euro; (https://www.numbeo.com/cost-of-living/in/Toulouse), rendering a total cost program of a total of ~1840&euro;, which is roughly $2250. According to skyscanner.com, a round-trip flight from Memphis to Toulouse from 06/21/18 to 07/22/18 will cost ~$1200, leaving my total program and trip costs to be an estimated $3450.
										</span>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Social justice pursuits appear as a pillar of my professional identity as a counseling psychologist, though there are often few opportunities for formal training in these pursuits, particularly at an international level. This program allows for opportunities to visit local schools, organizations, and mental health care professionals that will enable attendees to learn about social justice in a rapidly developing country. &nbsp;Through concerted training, mentorship, and experiential learning during the study abroad program&mdash;I hope to develop greater competency in applying the skills and expertise developed as a counseling psychologist to working with diverse groups. Additionally, embedding ourselves in diverse international communities allows developing psychologists to understand what access and barriers to mental health care are outside of the United States informing my work as a researcher and clinician. As our field moves towards globalizing psychology and providing mental health care for as broad of an audience as possible, knowing access and barriers to care will allow for practitioners in the field to create more comprehensive models of care and treatment that will likely serve the greatest number of people. Also, understanding what mental health care and traditional modes of treatment in Thailand may help inform culturally appropriate and competent care in my own research, education, and practice.<br />
<br />
&nbsp;<br />
<br />
The study abroad trip to Bangkok and Chiang Mai provide a unique opportunity in my training to experience and challenge my Westernized beliefs and values that are embedded in conceptualizations of American mental health education. My experiences travelling to Europe for leisure demonstrated the value of exposure and embeddedness in other cultures and communities as a way of experiential learning that allowed for greater understanding of my own values, beliefs, and norms beyond that of academic readings. It is my hope that attending the study abroad program will strengthen my awareness of self and expertise in working with diverse clients as well as developing skills in fostering and navigating professional international relationships that may arise in program development and research pursuits.<br />
<br />
&nbsp;<br />
<br />
Additionally, one of my research interests has involved understanding the loss experiences related to discrimination and victimization of transgender individuals as they navigate transitioning.&nbsp; In Thailand, conceptualization of gender identity appears distinct from a dichotomized, American understanding of gender. Being exposed to the ways in which trans* individuals navigate Thai culture and talking with individuals to see how this identity results in perceptions of gains and losses could greatly enhance my empirical work. Of similar importance, the time in the program will help illuminate the ways that gender and sexuality are constructed from a non-Western perspective and how this influences the rights of potentially marginalized populations.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>
										Studieninteressierte - Katholische Universit&auml;t Eichst&auml;tt-Ingolstadt, Eichstatt,Germany, Summer Term, Language Study<br />
Paris, France, 2 months, nanny for French family<br />

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am applying to participate with a unique partnership between the University of Memphis and the Simeto Community, in Sicily, Italy.&nbsp; This program represents an interdisciplinary partnership within the University of Memphis, between the City and Regional Planning Department and the Anthropology Department, as well as an international, multi-university partnership with students from UMass, Boston Graduate Program in Urban Planning and Community Development and Universita degli Studi di Catania in Sicily.&nbsp; This partnership provides an opportunity to work with the community members in the Simento River Valley on annual basis to implement a project&nbsp;contributing to the economic and environmental sustainability in this region. This year&#39;s project involves working with the community to create a plan for re-use of a historic building, previously a slaughter house.&nbsp;Specifically, the project involves an opportunity to work with community members to understand the historical context, social importance, and changing nature of community space.&nbsp; We are invited to examine the ways that the relationships between community members, local governmental leaders such as mayors and city leaders, and national government influence the creation and reshaping of community spaces. I believe this represents an opportunity to gain a deeper understanding of principles related to economic and environmental sustainability within the context of community partnership.&nbsp; As an anthropologist, I anticipate sharpening my skills in ethnographic research methods, participatory-action-research, and rapid assessment techniques through the engaged-learning process. Guidance for developing these skills will come from working under the mentorship of anthropology faculty member, Dr. Katherine Lambert-Pennington.&nbsp; Because this program involves working with a community which has a long history of positive partnership, I believe it will contribute to my overall goals of understanding solution-based research.&nbsp; &nbsp; I anticipate applying the skills I learn in my ongoing studies as well as future work as a researcher of human culture and experience.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										A big part of being able to mature as an individual and professional is understanding and acknowledging different perspectives. I think in life, it is so easy to get distracted from the truth that there is a world outside your own, and because of this being able to see situations from another perspective becomes difficult, and for some nonexistent. Outside of its&rsquo; academic purposes, I think a big purpose of study abroad programs are to facilitate an opportunity for students to become more aware and open to how others&rsquo; lives and their experiences formulate their worldview, and how they navigate through it. Though these experiences do not create the idea that now we know what others&rsquo; experiences are like, it does ideally give a sense of understanding and openness to continue to grow as an individual and remain open to the experiences of others. I am applying for this scholarship, because I have an interest in possibly doing social justice work internationally in the future, and I think this first experience traveling abroad will be a great introduction to the ideal of what social justice looks like on the international scale. Not only does this experience allow me to study abroad, which I have never had the opportunity to do before, but it also will be influential in understanding how I can make a difference internationally as a future psychologist. As I stated earlier, it is very easy to be consumed with your own life and experiences, especially when that it is all you know. I think this social justice class will require me to not only explore my own areas that I need growth but will also allow me to see how much bigger the world actually is, and how small some of the problems I have are compared to those around me. I think going to Thailand will be an experience within itself, because I have no previous experience working with clients that are involved with sex trafficking, but as this issue becomes more prevalent, I think it is important that I receive tools for working with this population, and I hope that Thailand can help me develop professionally in this way.&nbsp; This study abroad opportunity is important to my total program of study, not only because it meets my requirements for a Multicultural focused course, but also because it provides an opportunity for me to become a better therapist.&nbsp; By being exposed to a different culture and experience, it will require me to evaluate and even challenge my perspective and understanding of the world as my Memphis, TN worldview currently sees it. I am thankful for this opportunity to experience an opportunity to study abroad, because I think it will only strengthen me professionally as well as personally.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

									<td>

										<span>
										I decided to pursue my Master&#39;s in Journalism after realizing that I wanted to be an international investigative reporter. In my future career, I hope to travel to countries throughout the world. While in these countries, I hope to research and report on the different people of the world; specifically, I would like to draw attention to differences in lifestyle between countries. It is my belief that through my drawing attention to how drastically different each country is from the next and moreover, how different the United States is from essentially all other countries, people will have a better understanding and appreciation for people from different cultures.<br />
I decided to pursue studying abroad in Germany after realizing that the class, Media, Fake News and Right-wing Movements, related not only to my interests but also directly toward my future career. This class will explore the media of the United States and how it differs from other countries. This relates to my future career in that it explores how to be an American journalist while respecting and learning about other countries. Another reason I decided to pursue this program is because the class is taught by Dr. Tom Hrach, someone I consider to be a personal mentor.&nbsp;<br />
Having been abroad twice, I have learned the importance of listening to people from all cultures. It was only through these experiences abroad that I discovered so many parts of who I am. However, before, I went abroad only to enhance my own life. I had not yet discovered that I wanted to be an international investigative reporter at these times. I just knew that I wanted to go abroad because I felt it was important for my personal growth. Now, though, having a firmer grasp of what I want my future career to be, I feel it is imperative for me to go abroad and study journalism in a different culture.<br />
After having taken one of his classes, I&nbsp;know how deeply&nbsp;Dr. Hrach and&nbsp;his classes affect the thinking of his students. I am sure that that taking this particular class and it being offered by this particular professor will cause me to submerge myself in its contents. This submersion will cause me to look at the world around me in a new light, and in this case, the world around me will be different from the one I already know. This class, because of its subjects relating directly to my interests and future career, and this professor, because of his poignancy and personal effect on my life, will enable me to have a deeper, greater understanding of the culture I will be around. Thus, not only would I have a supreme abroad experience, but I also would have a stronger desire and drive to achieve my academic and career goals.
										</span>

									</td>

									<td>

										<span>
										The Paris Summer Institute is a five-week academic program in international and comparative law.  The Institute is cosponsored by Cornell Law School and Sorbonne Law School at the Universit√© Paris I Panth√©on-Sorbonne.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										Semester

										</span>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The legal profession, like most professions, has become increasingly globalized, which puts pressure on American lawyers to learn law in the international context. The Paris Summer Institute allows law students from across the world to broaden their legal knowledge for an increasingly globalizing age. This program not only provides the opportunity to make contacts and learn, but to do so in one of the most important centers of international law. The Paris Summer Institute, cosponsored by Cornell Law School and the Sorbonne Law School at the Universit&eacute; Paris I Panth&eacute;on-Sorbonne, is one of the best ways for law students to gain international legal experience. My decision to study abroad hinged on studying French, proximity to international political scene, and relevance for my career goals.<br />
I have studied French for the last year and a half, which has been enough to develop a vocabulary and command of the language that would benefit now by interactions with native French speakers. Studies demonstrate the value of the immersion method of learning a language, which has the potential supplement my language abilities, in addition to the formal French courses offered by the program. I am convinced of the benefit of having courses taught by experienced instructors and full immersion in French culture will be a great advantage in conducting professional relationships with French speakers throughout my career in moving me towards fluency.<br />
Additionally, the location of Paris is also very conducive to the study of international law. Paris has particularly had huge significance on a world scale from the Paris Climate Agreement to Versailles. Studying international law in the place where these developments occur is the kind of experience that cannot be replicated in any other location because it provides a context for the class lessons. For example, one of the courses offered is Case Studies on International Human rights, which France has played a major role in developing, such as the United Nations drafting the Universal Declaration of Human Rights in Paris. In addition, these developments are not only limited to France but also play a tremendous role in the United States&rsquo; ideas of jurisprudence and justice. For these reasons, Paris offers a uniquely beneficial location for the study of international law by close proximity to organizations and people working in world politics.<br />
Furthermore, I see the opportunities this program affords as a very important step in my career aspirations. The three main sectors of this field are business, government, and litigation, reflected in the courses: Comparative Corporate Law, International Human Rights, and International Arbitration and Complex Litigation. Each of these will provide an insight into the three main sectors of international law, as well as set up a framework for study of the American system of law in my studies at the University of Memphis. Moreover, the contacts and introduction into the network of international attorneys and businesses that this program brings has the potential to expand my job outlook after graduation in the United States, France, and around the world.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

tuition (US$3,750 - $4,750) and fees for language class (US$460), students are responsible for the cost of their own transportation to and from Paris, housing, meals, and other related expenses in Paris. 									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Last year was the first time I traveled to Europe. It was eye-opening to think that while I was living in the United States, used to the comfortable repetition of life, an entire world was happening, and I was missing it. I knew then, after seeing the rich culture and witnessing life in different parts of Europe, how important it was for me to learn more about the world and study music in a place outside of the United States.<br />
There were many reasons I selected the American Institute of Musical Study. One important one being the experiences and opportunities that I would be able to partake in while in this program. The core of my studies focuses around performance and is reliant on my ability to properly convey information and themes properly. While I have plenty of opportunity at the University of Memphis regarding performance opportunity, I seldom have a chance to be critiqued on my individual performance. I know that this program will afford me opportunities to meet with agents, and coaches daily, performing with large orchestras, and collaborating with other artists my age all which would help improve the way I communicate on stage. The second reason I chose this program was the application it provides as it pertains to my major. As a singer, I am required to sing in many languages and understand those languages. This program specifically aids students in learning German, a language which I have always struggled with, providing lessons and opportunities to be immersed in German culture. I also chose this program because of the fantastic teachers and musicians who I would be able to work with while in Austria. These individuals are from all over the world, many of whom I would not be able to come in contact with, without this opportunity. Their teaching, like that at the University of Memphis, would be invaluable to my studies. In addition to vocal lessons and coaching in German, I would have access to countless classes regarding my studies such as pedagogy, alexander technique, acting classes, stage combat classes, and much more.<br />
I wanted to pursue my master&rsquo;s degree at the University of Memphis because I am dedicated to excellence. I am hard working and talented and a program such as this will allow me to flourish with so many performance and learning opportunities. I am positive that these experiences will cross over into the work I do at the University and will help me become an improved and better-informed singer and community member for this school.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-6</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The overall cost of this program is $6,695. I have received a scholarship for this program totaling $2,850. The tuition for this progam includes room, one meal a day, and health insurance while in Austria. In addition to this they recommend an additional $1000-$1,500 for the remaining meals and transportation while at the program. I would also need an additional $1000 for airfare. I require no research support for this program, all material is provided prior to the start of this program.&nbsp;
										</span>

										<span>
										The program I am seeking the scholarship to support is the Social Work Study Abroad Program Summer 2018. This experience will grant me with an experience to obtain further knowledge about the profession of becoming a social worker on a global level to share with other colleagues upon my return. This program has allowed opportunities for future social workers to learn from other agencies across the world in how social workers incorporate the codes of ethics in their daily workforce for vulnerable populations. I am required to take courses such as Policy and Direct Practice with Organizations/ Communities as an undergraduate and graduate. Paris, France believes in equality for all people including the vulnerable populations such as the homeless and people with disabilities. This perspective is exhibited through policy and community. As I continued to participate in the curriculum for the summer, I could implement and identify the areas at which I learned from those courses. My research for the program will be to share the similarities and differences of services and how political and governmental influences change the lives of the people they serve.&nbsp;

										<span>
										<p><span style="font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 12px;">SUNY Purchase - Study Abroad Program - Madrid, Spain - 5 months<br />
European cities: Paris, Munich, Vienna, Saltzberg, Athens, Santorini 1-month, solo travel&nbsp;<br />
Mexico City - 2&nbsp; weeks - family vacation - many visits bet. 1979-2008<br />
Montreal - 3 days - vacation</span></span><br />

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Dear Study Abroad Committee,<br />
As a second language learner, I know all too well how fun, confusing, and embarrassing it can be learning another language. I have spent the greater part of my life learning Spanish in one form or another: hearing lullabies and songs from my mother, progressing to conjugating verbs in high school, reading Latin American literature in college, learning Spanish language and culture during a study abroad program in Madrid, and topping it off with a month-long immersion program in Mexico. I currently use my Spanish skills to translate at the IEI office. Learning Spanish has come with its rewards and challenges, I admit; however, as a New Yorker, who grew up in global city, I learned to appreciate how people from other nations navigate a hectic, often overwhelming city.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
Previously, I was an ESOL instructor for a community-based program in Queens and taught mostly undocumented immigrants from different parts of the world. It was a wonderful experience. With just a smattering of ESL background, I was able to dive in and get students to express themselves in English and have fun doing so. In addition, I worked for the ESL/Bilingual team of Macmillan/McGraw-Hill where I edited student and teacher editions of an ELL reading program called Treasure Chest. I was exposed to differentiated instruction, scaffolding and other concepts important to the English learner.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
The Pilsen program will add to those experiences and help me become an effective instructor and more well-rounded. It will provide a stronger understanding of what students actually go through, especially since the setting is EFL in the Czech Republic. It will be an excellent opportunity to get more hands-on experience with English learners. As a bonus, I want to discuss Franz Kafka and Milan Kundera with Czech students! Mostly, I want to continue building my instructional experience in ESL/EFL.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
I desire to participate in community building and encourage peer rapport, using authentic communication and materials in the classroom. Every classroom situation is different; consequently, as an ESL instructor, one must be responsive, open, and engaging. I am aware of my strengths: establishing rapport and lowering students&rsquo; affective filter; spontaneity is important to me. However, there is still so much to learn. I am confident I can be an asset to the program.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
I have heard former students rave about the Pilsen program, saying it was a fulfilling experiences. I know I will be well supported and nurtured. This is the kind of community I strive to be a part of.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
The study abroad experience will complement and contribute to my Master&rsquo;s in ESL concentration by exposing me to learners from the Czech Republic and offer me a foothold in being able to teach overseas. Upon completion, I will have a portfolio of work, a teaching philosophy, and much stronger skills; I will become a more confident ESL/EFL instructor. Like the other students who attended the Pilsen program, I feel it will be a fulfilling and exciting opportunity for me.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

									<td>

										<span>
										Receiving this scholarship would illustrate the university&rsquo;s investment and confidence in my abilities. Also it would show that the university wants to be active in my personal and professional growth. Currently, counseling psychology programs in the United States operate using a Westernized viewpoint of counseling. While this is suitable for the United States, the clientele which we serve is steadily becoming more diverse. This trip is an opportunity for me to observe cultures outside of the Western view to promote the best practices depending on the individual. Additionally, this trip would provide chances to interact with people that subscribe to ethics and moral codes different from those normed in the United States. Studying abroad in Thailand would potentially lead to constructing social justice efforts that could last and make an impact. In terms of my dissertation research, I believe that this excursion aligns with my interests in participatory action research. This involves getting in touch with community leaders and combining my knowledge of research to produce beneficial results for the population I&rsquo;m interested in. By reaching out to community leaders and working in the field, I can better understand the population and its customs.<br />
Through prior research, we are expected to encounter more collectivistic communities in Thailand. For example, the concept of leadership means something different here compared to what it would mean in an Eastern country. I would parallel this experience to the collectivistic cultures I work with in the United States, and hopefully this will lead to better and more efficient practices. Additionally, I would parallel this trip to representing a company or organization in a different country and working to establish international cohesion. Concerning further aspects of professional development and the program of study, traveling with some of my colleagues could foster productive collaboration. Having different points of views is beneficial for solving problems and for interpersonal reflection. Also, I would like to be a consultant psychologist for companies and organizations abroad, and traveling would increase my competency and exposure. I embrace being part of the University of Memphis Counseling Psychology program, and if granted the scholarship I would do my best to emulate the role of student, researcher, and consultant while hoping to bridge a connection for future international research.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

									<td>

										<span>
										I have had the distinct privilage of being selected to participate in the&nbsp;Accademia Vocale Lorenzo Malfatti Summer Vocal Intensive in Lucca, Italy this summer.&nbsp; I am thrilled to have been accepted into this prestigious program. It provides opportunities for substantial growth and development for young, aspiring opera singers, by allowing them to work with distinguished voice faculty. If I am able to attend this program, I will be able to expand my vocal knowledge and learn from teachers who have sung with some of the best opera companies in the world. This experience would be invaluable to my professional growth. As a first year masters student, it is time for me to begin applying to resident artist programs at opera companies, and the ability to participate inthis program would help me network with colleagues that can possibly help me find work in the future. I have been offered six hundred dollars in scholarship to be a young artist for this program, but I am still responsible for providing $4,000 for tuition and $2,000 for my flights. As a graduate student, this is not a feasable goal. I have 4 jobs to pay for school and rent and I will be unable to save this amount of money by June.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
I would be honored to be able to attend this program. I know that the ability to sing new repertoire, work with distinguished teachers and learn a language that is incredibly important to my craft. Throughout the rest of my career, 75% of my singing will be in Italian, so the opportunity to learn and sing in Italy would be incredible. T<br />
<br />
Thank you for your consideration.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

Secondly, there is an interest in opening up collaboration between UoM and Tianjin University engineering departments. My adviser, Dr. Qi, is interested in changing this and so is his correspondent in Tianjin.&nbsp;

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I became interested in the University of Memphis Counseling Psychology program due to the strong emphasis on social justice. Since beginning the program in August, it has been easy to see that social justice is not just a checklist for APA, but something that people are invested in. Part of my interest in going abroad and being a part of the trip to Thailand was to push myself personally and as an upcoming professional in the psychology world. A majority of this trip well be new experiences for me that will help me to begin to create a more international view of social justice.<br />
Additionally, this will be the first time I have ever traveled outside of the United States.&nbsp; I hope to be able to process this new experience with others who may be experiencing the same things as me along with others who have had experiences internationally. The ability to be surrounded others with a variety of experiences will allow all of us the opportunity to push out of our comfort zones and learn from one another in a country with values and standards different than our own.<br />
Part of being pushed out of my comfort zone will also include processing my own experiences and assess my areas of growth and notice the privileges I hold. Going to Thailand will assist me in developing an understanding of what life is like for individuals living in underdeveloped areas in Thailand. As a group, we will be experiencing various levels of developed areas from Bangkok as the most developed area to smaller villages with much less resources and opportunities. Not only will I begin to explore cultural differences from the United States to Thailand, but also from the more socially developed areas of Thailand to the impoverish areas.<br />
One of the major reasons I am excited to be attending this study abroad experience is exploring the views of mental health in Thailand. By going abroad and learning about how other cultures view mental health I am able to develop a greater understanding of how I can appropriately and adequately advocate for this population while remaining culturally sensitive to their needs. Additionally, I will be able to observe how environmental factors can influence and affect individuals overall well-being, specifically, their mental health. Advocating for individuals that live in areas with limited resources can be a difficult and educational experience and I am looking forward to experiencing and processing this with others that hold the same value in social justice as I do.<br />
Ultimately in this trip I am looking forward to being challenged and experiencing growth not only on a personal level, but on a professional level as well. I believe this experience will be a very challenging and humbling experience that will change the way that I view social justice and advocacy as a whole. I am grateful for this opportunity and the ability to have the experience with Dr. Ovrebo and students from several academic programs.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

									<td>

										<span>
										I&#39;m a graduate student in the musculoskeletal analysis laboratory. This class will help me integrate MATlab with a program that i already us visual 3D for biomechanical analysis of lower extremity to better understand the aging process, performance related variables. The process takes approximately 3-6 hours without the help of matlab, however, if i can code in matlab this will make the process to very quick (approximately 30 minutes). This will aid in productivity level of my work and research as i would like to continue studying lower extremity in various orthopedic conditions.&nbsp;

										<span>
										I have no previous international travel experience.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										ESMS 6902 will be taking place in the Biomechanics laboratory of the University of Hawaii-Manoa next summer (Summer 2018). During this course, we will be collecting 3D kinematic and kinetic data with motion-capture technology and then analyzing and processing the data in two specific programs: Visual 3D and Matlab. Learning how to code and program within these two softwares will make me a much more efficient and skilled scientist and, therefore, a more valuable asset to the University of Memphis. I have selected this program because my thesis will encompass every aspect covered in this course: 3D kinematics, kinetics, and Visual 3D processing aided by Matlab proficiency. The course will involve the analysis of data that includes neuromuscular activation patterns, mechanical outcomes of neuromuscular activation, and the summarization of this data through statistical methods. Each and every one of these items parallel the variables that I will be investigating in my thesis involving middle-aged runners and the protective effects of either a resistance training or gait retraining program.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

									<td>

										<span>
										To whom it may concern,<br />
<br />
When I was 15 years old, I got my first job as a teacher assistant at private School in Brazil. In the classroom, even at such a young age, I discovered that teaching was my vocation. Seeing then how a teacher can positively influence students&rsquo; lives helped me decide which career I would pursue throughout my life.<br />
<br />
In 2016, I applied for a master&rsquo;s Degree in Romance Languages ??at the University of Memphis.&nbsp; I was then awarded a full scholarship along with a TA position in the Spanish department with Professor Burgos.&nbsp;&nbsp; I am a very dedicated student, and this can be verified in my GPA 4.0.&nbsp; My main goal after graduation is to be a Spanish teacher for students from a public school in Greater Memphis.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
I am committed to learning so that I can in turn provide the best education possible to my students.&nbsp; Cultural immersion is a critical aspect to mastering a language and offers rich exposure to linguistic context and application.&nbsp; Study abroad is a wonderful opportunity and I greatly appreciate the support extended through the University of Memphis.&nbsp; If I did not have a young family, there is no doubt that I would pursue the four-week credit earning program offered in Madrid through the University of Memphis.&nbsp; Knowing a month is too long for my phase of life, and that I do not require the academic credits to graduate, I have sought out a more abbreviated two-week course program at Universidad Aut&ograve;noma de Barcelona, Spain focused on &ldquo;communicative language teaching used in our courses and reflecting on teaching Spanish to students from diverse backgrounds&rdquo;.&nbsp; This program is specifically tailored to build competence in teaching the Spanish language, including literary texts in the classroom, digital tools, classroom dynamics, etc.&nbsp; These topics are an ideal complement to my program of study and career in teaching.&nbsp; I hope that despite my limited circumstances that consideration would be given to this unique request and need for a shorter program.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
By reading the course description, I can already imagine myself learning there and bringing everything back to the classroom.&nbsp; This is also a unique opportunity to build relationships with other teachers with similar passions across the globe.&nbsp; I believe that this course will be an excellent complement to my training as a master&#39;s student and will also bring further credibility to my degree.&nbsp;<br />
<br />
Research shows that by 2050 the United States will be the country with more Spanish speakers than any other. &nbsp;I want to prepare myself as best I can to teach my students to learn a second language and even culture.&nbsp; This experience will help me to exemplify the importance of language in developing a broader perspective and the many rewarding opportunities that a language can unlock.&nbsp; And for that I count on the support of The University of Memphis Study Abroad Scholarship.<br />
<br />
Thank you for your support,<br />
<br />
Cristiana Moore<br />
<br />
Universidad Aut&ograve;noma de Barcelona - Teacher training for Foreign Teachers of Spanish.<br />
http://www.uab.cat/web/news-detail-1345709496023.html?noticiaid=1345741283715<br />
&nbsp;

										<span>
										I am seeking scholarship support for the Social Justice&nbsp;in Mental Health II program, as I am a graduate assistant who will be unable to embark upon this experience without it. The purpose of this program is to give students first hand experiences at dealing with international social justice issues and how to apply Counseling Psychology to the cause.&nbsp;This study abroad experience to Thailand is incredibly meaningful for me, as I have never been outside of U.S. territory. It will give me a glimpse into the lives of people who are less fortunate and allow me a firsthand experience within a culture different from my own. As part of my program of study, we must take courses that help us become multiculturally competent. Having that skill will aid in our understanding of our future clients&#39; needs and help us develop effective interventions. We must also be advocates for groups of people who are typically overlooked. To be able to advocate for those groups, we must have knowledge about the deficits faced within their cultures. What better way to learn about another culture than to become immersed within it? Professionally, it is imperative that I am culturally diverse and competent, and this experience will aid in my development of those competencies. My ultimate goal is to help at risk and less fortunate persons become the best possible versions of themselves and live productive lives. Understanding the needs of vast cultures of people and how to work with them will assist in fulfilling that goal. Having this study abroad experience to Thailand will begin my quest for knowledge in understanding the needs of and advocating for marginalized groups of people. It will also expose me to different cultural groups and help me to grow professionally as I pursue a career as a Counseling Psychologist.<br />
