										<span>
										The program I seek scholarship support for is the &ldquo;Sport, Commerce, &amp; Culture in the Global Marketplace&rdquo; program led by Dr. Brennan Berg of the Kemmons Wilson School of Hospitality and Resort Management.&nbsp; The reason I am applying for the study abroad scholarship is because I need financial support in order to be able to be apart of this program and I have selected this specific location and program because my major is Sport Commerce and Coventry University&rsquo;s School of Business in Coventry, England is ranked in the top five in the UK for Hospitality, Event Management, and Tourism. This study abroad experience will provide me with first-hand experience and an understanding of the dynamic global sport marketplace that is rapidly expanding. In my program of study I need to understand the dynamics of globalization and its impact on sport organizations today. In addition most sport organizations based in the United States must now be globally oriented to market their products and after this program I will be able to demonstrate to potential employers my appreciation of the broader global context in which sport organizations operate.&nbsp; This two week study abroad trip will be preceded by assigned course readings, assignments, and online discussions through eCourseware and the program will also include lectures by Coventry sport management faculty, leading global sport executives along with daily field visits to multinational enterprises involved in the management of global sport products, and group discussions led by Coventry University and University of Memphis faculty. With the study abroad scholarship I will be able to experience this trip that will greatly contribute to competence in the Sport Commerce major.&nbsp;<br />

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I have always wanted to study abroad, but had convinced myself time and time again throughout my undergraduate studies that it just wasn&rsquo;t the right time. I had heard from friends and strangers alike the benefits of studying abroad, but for some reason found myself putting it off to work more hours and save more money. However, I no longer wish to put off something that I have only thus far contemplated doing.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
The summer program in Lille was my choice because of not only my long-established interest in French language and culture, but also the international exposure the city itself offers. Different cultures funnel into the city making it a diverse and colorful environment to nourish both the wanderer and learner in me. Being one of the oldest established and the fifth largest in France, the city has a rich offering of history, as well as easily accessible travel by train to other notable areas, like Normandy, Paris, Brussels, and Amsterdam. Beyond my evident interest in France overall, these extras and cultural enhancements that Lille can afford me have been significant in my selection of program.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
I have been learning French for almost 10 years now and although it could be said I speak it at a near fluent level, it is only in a more formal, limited context, considering I have yet to be exposed to the language in a native setting. This trip would allow me to completely immerse myself in a language that I have worked extremely hard in thus far, earning my BA in it, and working towards my MA in it currently. It would not only greatly improve my speaking aptitude in the language, but also fine tune my listening skills with a variety of native speakers, improving my communication skills in the language, thus furthering my capacity for success in both my present MA program and a probable doctoral program post-graduation. With my MA program being mostly driven by the ability to teach a second language upon graduation, the experience of this trip would also better equip me to offer a more thorough language acquisition education to my future students.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
The chance to be in this program would ultimately enrich my current and future studies, my career goals, as well as afford me the ability to take on a new adventure I have yet to conquer &ndash; traveling not only outside the US for the first time, but also to a country where my chosen second language is spoken. I&rsquo;d like to thank you all in advance for your time and consideration in regard to this exciting opportunity.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am traveling to various parts of Thailand over the course of two weeks in May to learn more about social justice issues and how these issues are relative to the field of counseling. I spent two summers in Thailand during my undergraduate career at The University of Memphis. During those trips, I learned about the kindness of the people and the genuineness of their culture. I also grew in knowledge about the multitude of injustices that occur in Thailand, and I began to be more passionate in my pursuit to use my counseling skills and degree to help diminish those social injustices.<br />
<br />
This scholarship would help me advocate for those without a voice, as well as provide direction in the most helpful ways I can use my Master&rsquo;s degree. My long-term career plans include serving the Thai people through mental health awareness and offering tools and resources to end major injustices. I also hope to advocate for equality in the work force, family, and gender issues. However, my plans have no direction without further understanding and education on the current issues and the potential opportunities for growth.<br />
This scholarship will lend me the opportunity to strengthen my future vision for what counseling internationally looks like and where the greatest needs are. It would also assist me in gaining clarity for steps I can take within Tennessee and The UofM CMHC Program to educate and empower others towards preventing social injustice.<br />
<br />
This study abroad program is directly related to the field of Clinical Mental Health Counseling because the people we will encounter are in great need of advocacy, empathic listening, and resources to promote mental health. I would be so grateful to be a recipient of this scholarship.<br />
<br />
Thank you for your time and consideration.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

									<td>

										<span>
										Hello! My name is John Luke Reagan and I am an International MBA student on track to graduate in December of 2018. During my undergraduate career at the University of Tennessee, I decided to participate in a study abroad program in Malaga, Spain for the spring of 2016. The program was international business-based, and it was during this time period that I discovered that I have a passion for international business.<br />
This passion that grew within me lead me to apply to be a part of the International MBA program here at the University of Memphis. One thing that really attracted me to the IMBA program here is the opportunity to go abroad again. However, this time it would be more internship focused. Because of this requirement from the program, I have decided to apply for an internship opportunity in Valencia, Spain for the summer of 2018 as required by the International MBA program. As we all know, these types of internship programs do come with a cost.<br />
I chose Valencia because it is a hot-spot for international business, but there are other reasons as well. I have already studied in Spain, and would therefore like to put my work skills abroad to the test in the Spanish environment. The main attraction, however, would be an opportunity to improve my Spanish. I am already an advanced Spanish speaker, and I think that eight weeks in Spain would really allow me to get over the &quot;hump.&quot; Considering I have a Spanish focus in my IMBA program, I think the program in Valencia would be fitting.<br />
As one pursuing an International MBA, gaining work experience in an international environment and becoming more comfortable in a foreign language would do nothing but benefit my educational experience. Because of this, I hope that you choose me as a recipient for your scholarship. If chosen, I promise the deciding committee and anybody else associated with education at the University of Memphis that I will not let them down.
										</span>

									</td>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The program is approved by the American Bar Association and will allow me to earn up to six semester hours of law school credits by taking three courses for two credits each. &nbsp;The Courses offered this summer will be South Africa&rsquo;s Constitution, International Business Transactions, and International Human Rights. Further, the program will allow me to witness firsthand the historic legal and political changes in South Africa.&nbsp; As a result, I will get to participate in constitutional and other legal changes taking place in South Africa through this summer program.&nbsp;Additionally, guest lecturers in past programs comprise of South Africa&rsquo;s Minister of Finance, Minister of Justice, Minister of Provincial Affairs and Constitutional Development, Minister of Home Affairs, Constitutional and Supreme Court Judges and Members of Parliament. Also, a group of students in past had an opportunity to hear and meet President Barack Obama when he visited Cape Town through this program.<br />
Moreover, I&rsquo;m applying to this particular program because it is in a country in the infancy stage of democracy. Unlike America, its Constitution is not set in stone. Thus, I will actually get to see and gain a better understanding of how a constitution is crafted. Having a better understanding of the Constitution will be extremely beneficial for any law student or lawyer because it is the foundation of our legal system.<br />
In addition, I have a strong interest in international law and that course is being offered this summer. Upon graduation, I would like to work in a law firm here in the united states that deals with foreign clients or negotiating deals between clients located in two different countries. I would like to be either in-house counsel for a multinational company or as work as an attorney at a law firm with clients based in different countries all over the world. Currently, South Africa, is a resource-rich country, with a well-developed economy and an advanced technology base. Consequently, I believe South Africa will be a prime location for international business and transactions. Furthermore, now that South Africa&#39;s has moved to democracy there are new and untapped opportunities for international trade and commerce. I would like the chance to tap into these new opportunities by utilizing my future law degree coupled with the first-hand knowledge I will receive through participating in this program. &nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

A non-refundable registration fee (seat deposit) of $800 is due two weeks following your acceptance into the program. If you are applying after April 3, 2018, your seat deposit is due within forty-eight hours of your acceptance into the program. The registration fee will reserve your place in the program.<br />
The balance of $5690.00 is due by April 10, 2018. If there is a consortium agreement between your school and Howard University, then the balance of your fees is due ten days before the start of the program.&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<br />

									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am seeking scholarship support for the &ldquo;Social Justice in Mental Health II: Applications to International Contexts&rdquo; course that travels to Thailand. Social justice is a core value of my profession, counseling psychology, and me personally. Understanding multiculturalism and actively engaging in social justice are views that have been integrated throughout my academic experiences. As an undergraduate student, I selected coursework with service-learning components and chose to work at agencies that provided services to underprivileged families. As a graduate student, all of my classes encouraged cultural competence. For example, my diversity course further developed my passion for learning about intersectionality, identity development, and the systems of privilege and oppression. I learned the importance of continually developing an awareness of my own values, attitudes and assumptions with understanding the worldviews of others to be a conscientious psychologist. Now that I am engaged in a PhD program, I want to continue to develop my worldviews.<br />
<br />
Traveling and working internationally is a new opportunity for me to expand and grow professionally and personally. I want to go to Thailand specifically because of my interest in working with the lesbian, gay, bisexual, and trans* (LGBT) community. LGBT issues at the international level differ in a number of ways from here in the United States. For example, being trans* in other cultures, such as in Thailand, is not looked down upon or questioned. In fact, Thailand has an accepted third gender, unlike the binary construct that currently exists in the U. S. However, being LG or B in Thailand is extremely unacceptable whereas in the U. S. it is more widely accepted as compared to being trans*. Having the opportunity to explore this dynamic and understand how gender and sexuality are viewed in another culture will help influence my research as well as how I work with clients from other cultures. Additionally, as I identify as an advocate for this population I think it is extremely important for me to experience other cultures views so that I may more effectively assist individuals in this community find and have a voice.<br />
<br />
Counseling psychology as a profession also values working with the whole person and understanding how their identities impact who they are and their life circumstances. Having grown up and lived only in the U. S. I think it is important to take opportunities that expose you to cultures outside of the westernized view. Immersing myself into the collectivist society that is Thailand I believe I will gain a new insight into the world that will only benefit my future clients and research. I am extremely enthusiastic about this trip and look forward to the impact it will have on my professional and personal life.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>2-4</span>

									<td>

										<span>
										Growing up under the care of my Hungarian grandfather, I learned to celebrate cultural differences as he encouraged my curiosity in differing cultures, languages and customs. Thus, travel has always been a pursuit of mine. Once I reached an age where I managed my own finances, I prioritized travel within my budget.&nbsp; All trips (except those with an *) have been completely financially funded by me:
<ul>
	<li>San Jose, Costa Rica; Bagaces, Costa Rica : 2 weeks, homestay with locals I had met in high school (Dec 2012 - Jan 2013)</li>
	<li>Brno, Czech Republic : 6 months, undergraduate study abroad (2015)&nbsp;
	<ul>
		<li>visited: Dresden and Berlin, Germany; Prague, Oloumuc, Plzen and Karlovy Vary, Czech Republic; Budapest, Hungary; Bratislava, Slovakia; Krakow and&nbsp;Oswiecim, Poland; Amsterdam, Netherlands; Athens and Mykonos, Greece; Rome, Florence and Cinque Terre, Italy; Madrid, Barcelona and Pamplona Spain; Lisbon, Porto, Albufeira and Aveiro, Portugal</li>
	</ul>
	</li>
	<li>Lisbon, Portugal; Sintra, Portugal : 2 weeks, visiting friends from study abroad (2016)</li>
	<li>Roatan, Honduras : 2 weeks, post undergraduate trip with friends to become licensed open-water scuba divers</li>
	<li>Budapest, Hungary; Vienna, Austria; Maribor, Slovenia; Ljubljana, Slovenia; Zagreb, Croatia; Warsaw, Poland; Porto, Portugal : 1 month, solo trip after graduating undergrad (2016)</li>
	<li>Budapest, Hungary, 2 weeks, family vacation to visit the birthplace of my grandfather as well as connect with distant family (2017)*</li>
</ul>
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										The Simeto River Valley Agreement, which was granted 36 million euros for implementation by the European Union, is an innovative program that incorporates environmental, built, and economical planning. Each year, the agreement works with the Universities of Catania, Boston, and Memphis to make small but impactful projects come alive within these communities. The opportunity to work on a concrete project linking economic sustainability with socio-cultural and eco-environmental dimensions of development would allow me to bring relevant working knowledge back to Memphis where these elements are currently not a part of planning discourse. Like Memphis, Sicily is combating issues of economic and population decline, but unlike Memphis, growth is not the ideal focus for the Sicilians; rather, their focus is on resiliency within the proposed growth. Understanding the mechanics of their planning approach would shape my own within the Memphis community, an approach based off the mentality that planning is not merely a decision of today but the livelihood of tomorrow.&nbsp;<br />
The Sicilian community&rsquo;s relationship with the natural and built environment is intrinsic; for example, the Sicilians refer to the active volcano as Mamma Etna. Their engagement with place is personal and relational compared to our removed Memphian lifestyle. Place-making, the process of capitalizing on the assets, inspirations, and potentials of a local community to promote the overall well-being, health, and happiness of the residents, is a prominent tactical approach newly implemented within Memphis. I believe there is much to learn from a society that incorporates key elements of place-making within their culture.<br />
This program would provide me with the unique opportunity to incorporate my Bachelor of Arts, Linguistics, alongside my professional interest of international disaster mitigation and my personal interests of differing cultures, languages, and customs. Languages have always been an interest of mine. While I was raised practicing foreign language and customs, due to my Hungarian decent, my interest in both did not end there. While pursuing my bachelor&rsquo;s degree, I obtained at least elementary proficiency in Arabic, Portuguese, and Spanish. I have already begun a self-taught workbook to obtain a working elementary Italian vocabulary before the start of this program. I view language as one of many windows into better understanding people, culture, and place. As it is my hope to one day practice environmental planning on an international scale, I am currently working to obtain dual citizenship within Hungary. Not only would dual citizenship open professional opportunities, but it would allow me to have the opportunity to connect to my heritage.<br />
I have not had the opportunity to incorporate so many of my educational, professional, and personal interest into one program. Without this scholarship, I do not believe I can carry the full financial burden of this program. This scholarship would aid not only in equipping and empowering my education but also mold my individuality, mentality, and professionalism.<br />
<br />
<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>
										I have previously only been abroad for a family vacation in Canada in 1999. I believe this study abroad program will give me valuable cultural experience.&nbsp;
										</span>

								</tr>

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I am applying for this study abroad program because it provides a valuable new perspective on health law. Too often American legal thought is only influenced by what is occurring in the United States and what has previously occurred. As someone who is interested in health policy I think it is important to take into account what other countries are doing and how they are approaching their health systems. It is my hope to be able to use these program to understand how European countries handle their healthcare markets and regulate health policy.&nbsp;<br />
The programs allows students to study in European setting and learn European theories. It also provides opportunities for students to visit non governmental organizations and other players in the health field in France and Germany.<br />
I hope to be able to bring my experiences back and use them in my future career in health law. I also hope to provide information on what I learned to the University of Memphis Health Law and Policy Institute and Health Law Society. Informing fellow students of how European countries approach their health systems and how we can incorporate this knowledge is an important means to fixing our current problems.&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

I would estimate a financial need of $2,000 to help off set these costs.&nbsp;

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										I can say with absolutely certainty that when I decided to learn Spanish, and learn it fluently, my life changed for the better. It has shaped the way in which I view the world, other cultures, and the people I come into contact with on a daily basis. This may sound dramatic and over-exaggerated, but it&rsquo;s true. Learning the Spanish language changed me and taught me invaluable life lessons. Because of this, I want to share the lessons I have been taught and my appreciation for the Spanish language through teaching. My hope is that I will be able to ignite passion in at least one student I come into contact with, so that they too may one day pass it on to someone in their life.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;<br />
When thinking about passing on my passion for learning Spanish on to my students, I think about global competency. Ultimately, that is what all foreign language instructors hope to instill in their students, so they can carry a better appreciation for others with them as they embark on their own unique journeys in life. As a young black woman pursuing a master&rsquo;s degree in Spanish at the University of Memphis, I think it is especially important that other young black students (who make up a large percentage of the University&rsquo;s demographics), are able to see themselves when they see someone like me pursuing post graduate studies and aspiring to become a more well-rounded individual through experiences such as studying abroad. I believe rather firmly that global competency is made complete through an experience like studying abroad.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
As an individual who aspires to be a professor and to teach the importance of cultural awareness and cultural sensitivity, I believe that I will be better equipped to teach with an experience like traveling and studying in Madrid Spain. I wish to further my knowledge and deepen my understanding of the Spanish language by studying at the Universidad Complutense de Madrid. They have courses for graduate students that deal with how to teach Spanish as a foreign language, morphology, syntax, linguistics, and semantics, just to name a few. In addition to this, I will have the opportunity to explore the beautiful and illustrious culture of Spain, meet students from all walks of life and from all over the world, and be able to build lasting relationships. I will be able to bring real world materials and experiences to my classroom, which will greatly enhance the learning environment for the students I will be teaching next school year as a graduate assistant. This scholarship will also offer me an opportunity to travel without taking on a tremendous financial burden, during a crucial learning period in my graduate studies.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
Ultimately, receiving this scholarship will help me guide undergraduate students to understand the importance of studying other languages and cultures, so that they too may one day have the courage to venture out of their comfort zone and have culturally enriching and life-changing experiences. Thank you for your consideration.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>

The program I have selected provides focus in personal vocal technique, language skills, and acting, which all apply to my academic major. I am applying for a study abroad scholarship to help fund the tuition and travel costs associated with the program. Since I am married with two kids, the funds are very difficult to gather for a program of this nature. I have selected this particular program because it is directed/run by Benjamin Smith, the director of the opera program at the University of Memphis. &nbsp;

								<tr>
									<td class="compact-column">
										<span>2-5</span>
									</td>
									<td>

										<span>
										Studying abroad is far more than just changing the learning environment and taking a trip out of the country. It is important to experience the learning and training styles of other countries and other people because job, career, and educational&nbsp;opportunities have gotten so competitive. The world evolves so much an so fast, and it is important to stay updated with the latest information and innovations in your field of study. Sport is those activities that brings so many people and unique ideas together. Physically and emotionally people are connected, forced to build relationships, and work together as a team. Financially, some of the most expensive, but creative productions are put together for competition and entertainment. Sport is global, and studying abroad will give myself as well as my peers the opportunity to experience how sport along with its administration&nbsp;and finances&nbsp;is interpreted and applied at the international level. International players, fans, sponsors, and professionals of sport have to travel and be competent in all the subjects areas of the organizations in order&nbsp;to be productive and successful. Classroom learning and coursework is necessary however, I have been most successful with physical application of the principles and information that I have obtained. Sport is one of those things that forces relationship, whether that be business/professional or personal, nothing is going to make that networking and skill building easier that experience.
										</span>

									</td>
								</tr>

										<span>
										The study abroad program in the Simeto Valley region of Sicily supports an ongoing collaboration between area residents and three universities within the framework of an internationally renowned community development plan. Participation would afford me the opportunity to work on a meaningful, real-life project that involves many of the planning functions we have learned about in classes, including economic development, community organizing, and environmental sustainability. The program is a unique opportunity to be part of an ongoing body of work that has had a profound impact on the quality of life for area residents. It would also provide exposure to best practices at an international level, thus enabling me to bring new knowledge and new information to my future planning studies and practice.

										<span>
										Personal Statement<br />
&nbsp;<br />
Dear Scholarship support committee:<br />
My dream since childhood had always been to take care of other people in a hospitable manner. It is an interest I developed when I used to take care of my siblings most of the times when my parents were away.&nbsp; My interest further developed through reading various articles about hospitality and resorts management. I have loved to be an advocate for other people in an environment not familiar to them. It is this goal that has driven my past formal and informal studies in hospitality management. Further study in this area is likely to equip me with a final tool I might require to make my dream come true. Your scholarship support will assist me greatly as I push the wheel towards achieving my goal.<br />
My education and professional goal is to complete Masters Degree in Hospitality and Resorts management in the United States of America. Currently, I am conducting a research on hospitality and customer satisfaction which is relevant to my area of specialization.. I am ready to complete my Masters studies to enable me acquire the necessary skills and knowledge in this profession. I believe that with your scholarship support, I will be able to realize my dream.<br />
Staying in the UK for two weeks during study abroad allowed me to meet the industry representatives who mentored me in the field of hospitality. UK host students from all around the world and give them work placement either within the UK or abroad which I consider very helpful to me for career progression. Moreover, in the UK, there are tutors with high level of industry experience who are able to impart required skills that can assist a student like me to start own hospitality industry upon completion of the studies. These together with other factors have made me consider the UK as my preferred location to finish my Study abroad program.<br />
Furthermore, studying abroad closely relate to my area of profession since it will make me interact with people from various cultural backgrounds and with diverse experience in the field of hospitality and resorts management. Interacting with people of different cultures through learning will place me in a better position of establishing my own business as well as making me remain outstanding in the field of hospitality.&nbsp; It will be a way of making me competent and highly knowledgeable about international relations which is key in the carrier I am pursuing.<br />
As a student coming from a humble background, your scholarship support will be of great significance in propelling me to finish my Masters course. I am hoping to get a chance to proceed with my education through your scholarship support so that I can be an exceptional case to my family and society at large. I am hoping to be among those special people who will get your scholarship support and it is with great appreciation and honor that I submit my application for your consideration.<br />

									<td>

										<span>
										Former speaker of the House Tip O&#39;Neil was quoted as saying &quot;all politics is local,&quot;and usually, that statement is true. However, planning is more than local, because so many aspects of different cities are borrowed from others, and cities are milieus of various cultures. While the hands on experience that I have received at the University of Memphis has been excellent, certain aspects of planning can only be learned through travel, and exposure to different cultures. When I was considering Memphis for grad school, one aspect of the Urban Planning program stood out: the Environmental Planning and Design summer school in Sicily. Not only was there an opportunity to experience the planning process hands on in a major U.S. city, but that same hands on experience could be had in a new country, with different customs and perspectives on planning.<br />
<br />
Ultimately, my goals for this study abroad are to gain experience in a real world planning situation, and to expose myself to a different style of planning than the one common in the United States. Dr. Saija is originally from Sicily, and has the experience and relationships locally to provide us with the opportunity to be involved in this process. One traditional aspect of planning is that most cities hire firms that are not from the area, have very little experience locally, and expect them to come away with a plan that meets the needs of local constituencies. One of the consulting partners on the Memphis 3.0 plan, for example, is from Berkley, CA. This creates situations where planners have to learn the lay of the land incredibly quickly. Is there a better way to practice that than by going to another country, for a highly intensive school/workshop collaboration, for eleven days, and working on a project? The &ldquo;soft skills&rdquo; that grow from these sort of experiences, collaboration, communication, understanding, respect, are invaluable in the field of planning. On the other hand, planning is also a deeply theoretical field. Relationships between people and spaces they occupy define how one thinks about their community and their built environment. So many elements of US cities, sprawl, single family houses, suburban development, and the preference for those things, comes from how we understand space. One of the aspects that I&rsquo;m most looking forward to learning about is how Sicilans view space, and what that means for how they build. The town that we will be working in, Adrano, has about 35,000 people, and is mostly walkable, not only within itself, but with another town that is about two miles away, in contrast to many areas of Memphis, which most wouldn&rsquo;t consider walkable. Overall, I&rsquo;m excited for a chance to learn from people that are highly invested in their community, and hope to take away elements that I can use when I am working as a planner.<br />
&nbsp;
										</span>

									</td>
